⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وقالوا فيما يتعلق باليقظة : إن النفس قد تقوى على الانقطاع عن عالم الحس والاتصال بعالم الغيب والمتخيلة على استخلاص الحس المشترك عن الحواس الظاهرة، فتطلع على بعض المغيبات، وربما يكون ذلك بسماع صوت لذيذ أو هائل أو مكتوباً، أو تخاطباً من إنسان، أو ملك، أو جنى، أو هاتف غيب، وقد يقع بعض ذلك عند ضعف القوى الحسية لمرض أو مجاهدة، وعند دهشة الحس، أو تحير الخيال بمثل سرعة عدو، أو تأمل شفاف مرعش البصر، أو غلبة خوف، أو نحو ذلك . وبالجملة : فعجائب النفوس أظهر من أن تخفى وأكثر من أن تحصى. وأما الكلام في الأسباب. هذا هو القسم الثالث وهو غرائب تتعلق بالإدراكات حالة اليقظة. وذلك أن النفس قد تكون كاملة القوة، فتكتفي بالمتجاذبين، فلا يمنعها الاشتغال بتدبير الاتصال بالمبادىء، أي المجردات العلوية المفارقة والمتخيلة، أيضاً قد تكون قوية بحيث تقدر على استخلاص الحس المشترك عن الحواس الظاهرة، فلا يبعد أن يقع لمثل هذه النفس في اليقظة اتصال بالمبادىء، فينطبع فيها صور بعض المغيبات مما كان أو سيكون، ثم يفيض الأثر إلى المتخيلة، ثم ينتقل إلى الحس المشترك فربما يكون ذلك بسماع صوت لذيذ أو هائل، وربما يرد مكتوباً على لوح، أو تخاطباً من إنسان، أو ملك، أو جنى، أو هاتف غيب، أو نحو ذلك، وقد يكون مشاهدة صور ما لا حضور له عند الحس، لا لشرف النفس وكمال قوتها بل لفساد في الآلات التي يستعملها العقل، كما في المرض والجنون، أو لاستيلاء أمر يدهش الحس، ويحير الخيال، كالعدو سرعة، وكتأمل شيء شفاف مرعش للبصر، مدهش إياه الشفيفة، كسواد براق، أو لغلبة خوف أو ظن، أو وهم تعين التخيل، وقد يكون ذلك بالرياضات المضعفة للقوى العائقة للنفس عن اتصالها بالمباديء الجاذبة إياها إلى جانب السفليات، إلى غير من الأسباب المؤثرة عند الفلاسفة والعادية عندنا والخالق هو الله تعالى. إن الذين قالوا ربنا الله ثم استقاموا تتنزل عليهم الملائكة ألا تخافوا ولا تحزنوا وابشروا بالجنة التي كنتم توعدون، نحن أولياؤكم في الحياة الدنيا وفي الآخرة ولكم فيها ما تشتهي أنفسكم ولكم فيها ما تدعون نزلاً من غفور رحيم
He said: And they said regarding wakefulness: The soul may become strong in disconnecting from the world of sense and connecting to the world of the unseen, and the imaginative faculty in withdrawing the common sense from the external senses, so it gains knowledge of some hidden things. Perhaps that occurs by hearing a pleasant or terrifying voice, or a written form, or speech from a human, an angel, a jinn, or an unseen caller. And some of that may occur due to weakness of the sensory powers from illness or spiritual struggle, and due to astonishment of the sense, or confusion of the imagination such as from the speed of an enemy, or from contemplation of a transparent thing that dazzles the sight, or from overwhelming fear, or the like. In summary: the wonders of souls are too apparent to be hidden and too numerous to be counted. And as for speech about the causes: This is the third section, which is wonders related to perceptions in the state of wakefulness. That is, the soul may be complete in power, so that occupation with managing the body does not prevent it from connecting to the principles—i.e., the separated higher abstract entities—and the imaginative faculty. Also, it may be strong in that it can withdraw the common sense from the external senses, so it is not improbable that for such a soul in wakefulness there occurs a connection to the principles, and there are imprinted in it images of some hidden things—what was or will be—then the effect flows to the imaginative faculty, then transfers to the common sense. So perhaps that is by hearing a pleasant or terrifying voice, and perhaps it comes as writing on a tablet, or speech from a human, an angel, a jinn, or an unseen caller, or the like. And it may be the observation of images of what is not present to the sense, not due to the nobility of the soul and perfection of its power but rather due to corruption in the instruments that reason uses, as in illness and madness, or due to the domination of an affair that astonishes the sense and confuses the imagination, such as the speed of an enemy, and such as contemplating a transparent thing that dazzles the sight, astonishing it with its transparency, like a gleaming blackness, or due to overwhelming fear or conjecture or illusion that determines imagination. And that may occur through spiritual exercises that weaken the forces that hinder the soul from its connection to the principles that attract it to the side of lower things, and other such causes that are effective according to the philosophers, while for us the ordinary cause, and the Creator is Allah, the Exalted. Indeed, those who have said 'Our Lord is Allah' and then remained steadfast, the angels descend upon them, saying, 'Fear not, nor grieve, and receive good tidings of Paradise which you were promised. We are your allies in the worldly life and in the Hereafter. And therein you will have whatever your souls desire, and therein you will have whatever you call for, as hospitality from a Forgiving, Merciful One.'

Commentary
This passage discusses waking perceptions of the unseen. The author begins by stating that the soul can be so strong that it disconnects from the sensory world and connects to the unseen, with the imaginative faculty drawing the common sense away from the external senses, thus gaining knowledge of certain hidden things. This may occur through hearing a pleasant or terrifying voice, or through a written form, or through speech from a human, angel, jinn, or unseen caller. The author then explains that this can also happen due to weakness of the senses from illness or spiritual struggle, or due to astonishment of the senses or confusion of the imagination from fast running, or gazing at a transparent object that dazzles the sight, or overwhelming fear, etc. He summarizes that the wonders of souls are too obvious to hide and too many to count. He then adds that this is the third section—wonders related to perceptions in wakefulness. He further explains that the soul may be complete in power, so that occupation with managing the body does not prevent it from connecting to the higher abstract entities and the imaginative faculty. Or the soul may be strong in a different way, able to withdraw the common sense from the external senses, and then in wakefulness it connects to the principles, imprinting images of some hidden things—past or future—which then flow to the imaginative faculty and then to the common sense, resulting in hearing or seeing things. This can also occur not due to the soul's strength but due to corruption of the instruments used by reason, as in illness or madness, or due to an overwhelming factor that dazzles the senses and confuses the imagination. It can also occur through spiritual exercises that weaken the forces that hinder the soul from connecting to the principles that attract it to lower things. The author concludes by noting that these are causes according to philosophers, while for us (Muslims) the real cause is Allah, the Creator, and he cites a Quranic verse about angels descending on the righteous.

Extraordinary Perceptions in Wakefulness: Causes and Types
Taftazani enumerates the causes of extraordinary perceptions in wakefulness: soul's strength, bodily defects, and spiritual exercises.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that extraordinary perceptions in wakefulness can arise from two main causes: the soul's strength and connection to higher principles, or from defective bodily states, and that spiritual exercises can also facilitate this connection.

Core Idea
Extraordinary wakeful perceptions can stem from a powerful soul or from bodily defects, but both are under Allah's creation.

This passage introduces the third category of wonders—extraordinary perceptions that occur while awake. The author explains that such perceptions are not merely products of madness or fantasy. Rather, they can be genuine experiences resulting either from the soul's strength enabling it to connect with higher spiritual realms, or from temporary dysfunctions in the sensory apparatus. Additionally, spiritual practices can weaken bodily attachments, allowing the soul to perceive hidden realities. This lesson will guide you through these causes and their implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the two broad categories of causes mentioned.
The passage begins by stating this is the third section.
2
Identify the mechanism of the strong soul
Focus on the description: the soul's power allows it to simultaneously manage the body and connect to higher principles. Trace the flow of information from principles to imaginative faculty to common sense, manifesting as voices, writings, or speeches.
The author lists various manifestations like hearing a voice or seeing writing on a tablet.
3
Recognize defective causes and the role of spiritual exercises
The passage then lists causes like illness, madness, fear, and dazzling sights. It also mentions spiritual exercises that weaken hindering powers. Note that these causes are considered 'customary' in our theological framework, while the ultimate creator is Allah.
The Quranic verse at the end serves as a proof that such perceptions can occur.

This is the third section, which is wonders related to perceptions in the state of wakefulness. That is because the soul may be complete in power, so it suffices with the two opposing forces, and preoccupation with managing the body does not prevent it from connection to the principles, i.e., the separate higher spiritual beings and the imaginative faculty. Also, it may be strong enough to extract the common sense from the external senses, so it is not unlikely that for such a soul in wakefulness there occurs a connection to the principles, and then images of some hidden things (غيب) of what was or will be are imprinted in it, then the effect flows to the imaginative faculty, then transfers to the common sense. So perhaps that is by hearing a pleasant or terrifying voice, and perhaps it comes written on a tablet, or as a speech from a human, or an angel, or a jinn, or a hidden caller (هاتف غيب), or the like. And it may be seeing images of what is not present to the senses, not due to the nobility of the soul and perfection of its power, but due to corruption in the instruments that the intellect uses, as in illness and madness, or due to the domination of a matter that astonishes the senses and confuses the imagination, like the speed of an enemy, or examining something transparent that dazzles the sight, stunning it with its transparency, like a shining blackness, or due to the overwhelming of fear or suspicion, or a fancy that determines the imagination. And it may be through spiritual exercises that weaken the powers that hinder the soul from its connection to the principles that attract it to the lower side, and other effective causes according to the philosophers, and (which are) customary with us, while the Creator is God Almighty. 'Indeed, those who have said, "Our Lord is Allah," and then remained steadfast – the angels descend upon them, [saying], "Fear not nor grieve, but receive good tidings of Paradise, which you were promised. We are your allies in the worldly life and in the Hereafter. And therein you will have whatever your souls desire, and therein you will have whatever you call for, as a hospitality from the Forgiving, Merciful."' (Surah Fussilat, verses 30-32).
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the third category of wonders: extraordinary perceptions that occur in the state of wakefulness. The author begins by stating that this is the third section. He then explains that the soul may be so powerful that it can simultaneously attend to the body and connect to higher principles (المبادىء), i.e., the separate spiritual beings (المجردات العلوية المفارقة) and the imaginative faculty. Alternatively, the soul may be strong enough to separate the common sense from the external senses, allowing it to receive impressions from the higher world. When this happens, images of unseen things (المغيبات) — past or future — are imprinted in the soul, then pass to the imagination, then to the common sense. This may manifest as hearing a voice, seeing writing on a tablet, or receiving speech from a human, angel, jinn, or a hidden caller. The passage notes that such perceptions can also arise from defective causes, such as illness, madness, intense fear, or dazzling visual phenomena. Additionally, spiritual exercises that weaken bodily attachments can facilitate this connection, though these causes are considered 'customary' (عارية) in our framework, while the ultimate creator is God. The passage concludes by quoting Quran 41:30-32 as an example of angels descending upon the steadfast, supporting the possibility of such extraordinary perceptions.

Do Animals Have Immaterial Souls?
Presents the debate on animal souls with three positions and evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three main positions on whether animals have immaterial souls and the rational and revealed arguments for affirming them.

Core Idea
Animals' intelligent behaviors may point to immaterial souls, but scholars disagree.

This passage presents a fascinating kalam debate: do animals have immaterial souls? The author outlines three positions and then focuses on the rational and scriptural evidence used by those who affirm animal souls. As you read, note how the argument from 'universal perceptions' is key to the rational case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
Read the passage and list the three views: (1) majority of philosophers deny, (2) some suspend judgment, (3) a group affirms based on reason and revelation.
The author refutes an objection to the third view.
2
Examine the rational evidence
Look at the examples given: bees, ants, animals finding way, elephants, birds treating illness. Why do these indicate 'universal perceptions'?
3
Consider the transmitted evidence
Identify the Quranic verses cited (24:41, 16:68, 34:10). How do they support animal souls?
4
Reflect on the author's stance
The author does not fully endorse any view but presents the evidence. How does he frame the debate?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ووقوع بعض الغرائب من الحيوانات الأخر على ما تقرر في علم الحيوان، وربما يشهد بأن لها أيضاً نفوساً مجردة، والعلم عند الله. ذهب جمهور الفلاسفة، إلى أنه ليست لغير الإنسان من الحيوانات، نفوس مجردة، مدركة للكليات وبعضهم إلى أنا لا نعرف وجود النفس لها لعدم الدليل ولا نقطع بالانتفاء لقيام الاحتمال وما يتوهم من أنه لو كانت لها نفوس، لكانت إنساناً، لأن حقيقته النفس والبدن لا غير، ليس بشيء، لجواز اختلاف النفسين بالحقيقة، وجواز التميز لفصول أخر لا يطلع على حقيقتها، وذهب جمع من أهل النظر إلى ثبوت ذلك تمسكاً بالمعقول والمنقول. أما المعقول. فهو أنا نشاهد منها أفعالاً غريبة تدل على أن لها إدراكات كلية، وتصورات عقلية، كالنحل في بناء بيوته المسدسة، والانقياد لرئيس والنمل في إعداد الذخيرة، والإبل والبغل والخيل والحمار في الاهتداء إلى الطريق في الليالي المظلمة، والفيل في غرائب أحوال تشاهد منه، وكثير من الطيور والحشرات في علاج أمراض تعرض لها، إلى غير ذلك من الحيل العجيبة التي يعجز عنها كثير من العقلاء، وأما المنقول فكقوله تعالى والطير صافات كل قد علم صلاته وتسبيحه وقوله تعالى وأوحى ربك إلى النحل الآية. وقوله تعالى يا جبال أوبى معه
He said: And the occurrence of some wonders from other animals, as established in zoology, and perhaps it witnesses that they also have immaterial souls, and knowledge is with God. The majority of philosophers went that non-human animals do not have immaterial souls that perceive universals. And some (went) that we do not know the existence of a soul for them due to lack of evidence, and we do not definitively negate it due to the existence of possibility. And what is imagined — that if they had souls, they would be human, because the reality of a human is nothing but soul and body — is not valid, because it is possible for two souls to differ in reality, and for distinction by other differentiae whose reality is not known. And a group of the people of reflection (أهل النظر) went to affirming that, adhering to the rational (المعقول) and the transmitted (المنقول). As for the rational: we witness from them strange actions that indicate that they have universal perceptions (ادراكات كلية) and rational conceptualizations (تصورات عقلية), like the bee in building its hexagonal houses and obedience to a leader, and the ant in preparing provisions, and the camel, mule, horse, and donkey in finding the way in dark nights, and the elephant in strange conditions observed from it, and many birds and insects in treating diseases that occur to them, and other amazing stratagems that many rational people are incapable of. As for the transmitted: like His statement, the Exalted, 'And the birds, spreading [their wings]; each has known its prayer and its exaltation' (Quran 24:41), and His statement, the Exalted, 'And your Lord inspired to the bee' (Quran 16:68), and His statement, the Exalted, 'O mountains, repeat [praises] with him' (Quran 34:10).
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage addresses a debated question in kalam: whether animals other than humans have immaterial souls (النفوس المجردة). The author begins by noting that some wonders observed in animals may witness to their having such souls, but knowledge ultimately rests with God. He then reports three positions: (1) The majority of philosophers deny that animals have immaterial souls that perceive universals. (2) Some suspend judgment, neither affirming nor denying due to lack of conclusive evidence. The author refutes the objection that if animals had souls they would be human, by arguing that souls can differ in reality and there may be other differentiae. (3) A group of theologians (أهل النظر) affirm animal souls, based on both rational and revealed evidence. The rational evidence includes observable intelligent behaviors such as bees building hexagonal cells, ants storing food, animals finding their way in darkness, and birds treating their illnesses—actions that imply universal concepts and reasoning. The revealed evidence includes Quranic verses that attribute prayer, praise, and divine inspiration to animals, suggesting they have spiritual awareness.

Key Terms
نفوس مجردة
المعقول
المنقول
ادراكات كلية
تصورات عقلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If animals had souls, they would be human.
Correction: The author argues that souls can differ in reality, and there may be other differentiae, so animal souls do not make them human.

Checkpoint
What is the main rational argument presented by those who affirm animal souls?
A) Animals have physical bodies like humans
B) Animals perform complex actions that indicate universal perceptions
C) Animals can speak
D) Animals have emotions

Key Takeaway
The debate over animal souls hinges on whether their actions require immaterial cognition; some scholars argue yes based on reason and revelation.

?

?

?
You have been given a soul with universal perception and rational conceptualization, unlike animals which may have a lesser soul. What are you doing with this gift? Will you use it to know your Creator and obey Him, or are you burying it under worldly distractions? Name one step you will take this week to harness your intellect for spiritual growth.

Three Opinions on Animal Souls
Al-Taftazani reports opinions and refutes an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three main Islamic philosophical positions on whether animals have immaterial souls and the refutation of a common objection.

Core Idea
Animal souls: denied by most philosophers, uncertain by some, affirmed by kalam scholars.

Al-Taftazani opens the discussion on animal souls by presenting the range of opinions among philosophers and theologians. He first notes that wondrous animal behaviors may hint at immaterial souls, then reports the views of the majority of philosophers, a skeptical group, and finally the scholars of kalam who affirm it. He also refutes an objection that would collapse the distinction between humans and animals.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening claim
Notice how Al-Taftazani introduces the possibility of animal souls by referencing wonders in zoology.
He does not assert it outright but presents it as witnessing.
2
Identify the three opinions
Look for the three groups: majority philosophers (deny), some (withhold judgment), and kalam scholars (affirm).
The kalam scholars rely on both rational and transmitted proofs.
3
Understand the refutation
Read the objection that animal souls would make them human, and note how Al-Taftazani refutes it by allowing differing essences and unknown differentiae.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ووقوع بعض الغرائب من الحيوانات الأخر على ما تقرر في علم الحيوان، وربما يشهد بأن لها أيضاً نفوساً مجردة، والعلم عند الله. ذهب جمهور الفلاسفة، إلى أنه ليست لغير الإنسان من الحيوانات، نفوس مجردة، مدركة للكليات، وبعضهم إلى أنا لا نعرف وجود النفس لها لعدم الدليل ولا نقطع بالانتفاء لقيام الاحتمال، وما يتوهم من أنه لو كانت لها نفوس لكانت إنساناً، لأن حقيقته النفس والبدن لا غير، ليس بشيء، لجواز اختلاف النفسين بالحقيقة، وجواز التميز لفصول أخر لا يطلع على حقيقتها. وذهب جمع من أهل النظر إلى ثبوت ذلك تمسكاً بالمعقول والمنقول. أما المعقول: فهو أنا نشاهد منها أفعالاً غريبة تدل على أن لها إدراكات كلية وتصورات عقلية، كالنحل في بناء بيوته المسدسة، والانقياد لرئيس، والنمل في إعداد الذخيرة، والإبل والبغل والخيل والحمار في الاهتداء إلى الطريق في الليالي المظلمة، والفيل في غرائب أحوال تشاهد منه، وكثير من الطيور والحشرات في علاج أمراض تعرض لها، إلى غير ذلك من الحيل العجيبة التي يعجز عنها كثير من العقلاء.
He said: The occurrence of some wonders from other animals as established in zoology may also witness that they likewise have immaterial souls, and knowledge is with God. The majority of philosophers held that animals other than humans do not have immaterial souls that perceive universals. Some held that we do not know the existence of the soul for them due to lack of proof, nor do we definitively negate it due to the existence of possibility. And the misconception that if they had souls they would be human, because his essence is soul and body only, is nothing, because the two souls may differ in essence, and it is possible to distinguish by other differentiae whose reality is not known. A group of scholars of kalam went to affirming that, adhering to the rational and the transmitted. As for the rational: it is that we witness from them strange actions that indicate that they have universal perceptions and intellectual conceptualizations, like the bee in building its hexagonal houses and submission to a leader, the ant in storing provisions, the camel, the mule, the horse, and the donkey in finding the way in dark nights, the elephant in strange states witnessed from it, many birds and insects in treating illnesses that befall them, and other wondrous stratagems that many rational people are incapable of.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage argues for animal souls through rational observation. It begins by noting that strange phenomena in animals may indicate they have immaterial souls. Then it reports three opinions: (1) the majority of philosophers deny animal souls perceiving universals; (2) some withhold judgment due to lack of evidence; (3) a group of kalam scholars affirm it based on rational and transmitted proofs. The author refutes an objection that if animals had souls they would be human, since the human essence is soul and body; he argues that souls can differ in essence and be distinguished by unknown differentiae. The rational proof lists observable animal behaviors that imply universal perception and intellectual conceptualization: bees building hexagonal hives, ants storing food, animals navigating dark nights, birds and insects treating diseases, etc. These wonders, he says, are beyond many rational humans.

Key Terms
نفوس مجردة
مدركة للكليات
أهل النظر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If animals had souls, they would be human beings.
Correction: Souls can differ in essence, and there can be other distinguishing features (differentiae) that prevent animals from being human even if they have souls.

Checkpoint
What is the position of the majority of philosophers on animal souls?
A) They affirm that animals have immaterial souls.
B) They deny that animals have immaterial souls that perceive universals.
C) They withhold judgment.
D) They believe animals have material souls.

Key Takeaway
The debate on animal souls involves three main positions, with the kalam scholars affirming based on rational evidence, and a key objection refuted by allowing soul essences to differ.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Rational Evidence from Animal Behavior
Al-Taftazani presents rational proof examples for animal souls.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will recognize how specific animal behaviors, such as bees building hexagonal hives and ants storing food, are used as rational evidence for animal souls.

Complex animal behaviors imply universal perception and intellectual conceptualization.

He lists a series of striking animal behaviors that seem to require more than mere instinct, suggesting that animals possess some form of universal perception and intellect. 3

This strengthens the argument for animal intellect.

Quranic Evidence for Animal Souls
Al-Taftazani lists five Quranic verses as transmitted proofs for animal souls.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Taftazani uses five specific Quranic verses as transmitted proofs to establish that animals have immaterial souls capable of knowledge, intention, and communication.

Core Idea
The Quran describes animals glorifying Allah, receiving inspiration, and reasoning—proof of their souls.

Having discussed rational arguments, al-Taftazani now turns to transmitted (naqli) evidence from the Quran. He cites five verses that attribute to animals actions like prayer, glorification, inspiration, and logical reasoning. These attributes imply the presence of a soul that enables such acts. This lesson examines each verse and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage

The verses are presented in sequence without commentary.
2

For each verse, note what action or quality is attributed to the animal (e.g., knowing prayer, receiving inspiration).
3
Understand the logical inference
Reflect on why each attributed action implies a soul. For example, knowing prayer requires understanding and intention.
The commentary explains the connection.
4
Consider the cumulative proof
Think about how all five verses together strengthen the case for animal souls beyond a single verse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المنقول: فكقوله تعالى: (والطير صافات كل قد علم صلاته وتسبيحه) وقوله تعالى: (وأوحى ربك إلى النحل) الآية، وقوله تعالى: (يا جبال أوبى معه والطير) وقوله تعالى حكاية عن الهدهد: (أحطت بما لم تحط به) الآية، وحكاية عن النملة: (يا أيها النمل ادخلوا مساكنكم) الآية.
As for the transmitted: like His statement, the Most High: 'And the birds spreading their wings. Each one has known its prayer and glorification' (Quran 24:41), and His statement, the Most High: 'And your Lord inspired to the bee' (Quran 16:68) the verse, and His statement, the Most High: 'O mountains, repeat with him and the birds' (Quran 34:10), and His statement, the Most High, narrated from the hoopoe: 'I have encompassed what you have not encompassed' (Quran 27:22) the verse, and narrated from the ant: 'O ants, enter your dwellings' (Quran 27:18) the verse.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage provides the transmitted (naqli) proofs for animal souls, specifically from the Quran. It cites five verses: (1) Quran 24:41, stating birds know their prayer and glorification, implying knowledge and intention; (2) Quran 16:68, where God inspires the bee, indicating divine communication; (3) Quran 34:10, where God addresses mountains and birds to glorify with David; (4) Quran 27:22, where the hoopoe reports knowledge beyond Solomon's, showing intellectual perception; (5) Quran 27:18, where the ant warns its community, indicating reasoning and communication. These verses are presented as evidence that animals possess souls capable of knowledge, understanding, and even revelation-like inspiration.

?

The Ten Intellects: Number and the Role of the First and Tenth
Explains the number of intellects and the roles of the first and tenth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the intellects are stated to be ten, the specific roles of the first and tenth intellects, and the possibility of there being more intellects beyond ten.

Core Idea
The ten intellects are a lower limit, not an exact count; only Allah knows the true number.

This passage from Sharh al-Maqasid addresses a key doctrine of the Peripatetic Muslim philosophers: the number of separate intellects. The author argues that the intellects are at least ten, corresponding to the nine spheres plus the First, but leaves open the possibility of more. The passage also distinguishes the role of the tenth intellect as the manager of the sublunary world and describes the attributes of all intellects.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the English translation. Pay attention to the flow: the claim about ten intellects, the description of the tenth, and the justification for the number.
The passage is dense; read slowly and note the key terms.
2
Identify the claim about the number
The passage states that the intellects are ten 'after the First, negating the side of fewness, not abundance.' Understand that this means ten is a minimum, not an exact count.
The author explicitly says more are possible and only Allah knows the true number.
3
Understand the roles of the first and tenth intellects
The first intellect is the source from which the spheres and their intellects emanate. The tenth intellect is the manager of the elemental (sublunary) world, bestowing perfections based on celestial configurations.
The tenth intellect's management is through effusion, not bodily governance.
4
Reflect on the attributes of the intellects
The passage notes that the intellects are eternal, free from matter, their species restricted to individuals, and they intellect universals but not particulars.
These attributes are foundational for understanding the intellects' role in causality and knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث الثاني في أحواله : زعموا أنها عشرة بعدد الأفلاك بعد الأول نفياً لجانب القلة دون الكثرة والعاشر هو المدبر لعالم العناصر بحسب الاستعدادات الحاصلة من تجرد أوضاع الأفلاك، وأنها لبراءتها عن المادة، حلولاً وتعلقاً أزلية منحصرة أنواعها في أشخاصها جامعة لكمالاتها، عاقلة لذواتها، ولسائر المجردات، بل لجميع الكليات دون الجزئيات . يشير إلى إثبات أحكام تتفرع على إثبات العقول المجردة منها، أنها عشرة. بمعنى أنها ليست أقل من ذلك. وأما في جانب الكثرة فالعلم عند الله تعالى. كيف ولا قطع بانحصار الأفلاك الكلية في التسع، بل يجوز أن يكون بين الفلك المحيط بالكل، وفلك الثوابت أفلاك كثيرة ، وأن يكون كل من الثوابت في فلك . ولو سلّم فيجوز أن يكون لكل من الأفلاك الجزئية عقل يدبر أمره، ويتشبه هو به بوجه لا يعلم كنهه إلا الله تعالى وحده، وإنما تصير عشرة مع كون الأفلاك تسعة . لأن الأول مصدر لفلك، ونفس ، وعقل، وهكذا إلى الآخر، فتكون العقول الصادرة تسعة ، ومع الأول المصدر عشرة، والعاشر الذي هو عقل الفلك الأخير يدبر أمر عالم العناصر بحسب الاستعدادات التي تحصل للمواد العنصرية، من تجدد الأوضاع الفلكية. والمراد بتدبير العقول التأثير وإفاضة الكمالات لا التصرف الذي للنفوس مع الأبدان
The second investigation concerning their states: They claimed that they are ten according to the number of the spheres, after the First, negating the side of fewness, not abundance; and the tenth is the manager of the world of elements according to the dispositions resulting from the immateriality of the configurations of the spheres; and that they, by virtue of being free from matter—whether by indwelling or attachment—are eternal, their species are restricted to their individuals, they possess their perfections actually, they are intellective of themselves and of the rest of the immaterial entities, indeed of all universals but not of particulars. He indicates the establishment of rulings that branch off from the establishment of the immaterial intellects, among them that they are ten—meaning they are not less than that. As for the side of abundance, knowledge belongs to God most high. How? There is no certainty that the universal spheres are restricted to nine; rather, it is possible that between the all-encompassing sphere and the sphere of the fixed stars there are many spheres, and that each of the fixed stars is in a sphere. And even if that is conceded, it is possible that for each of the particular spheres there is an intellect that manages its affair and is assimilated to it in a way whose reality is known only to God most high. They become ten despite the spheres being nine because the First is a source for a sphere, a soul, and an intellect, and so on until the last; thus the emanating intellects are nine, and together with the First Source they are ten. The tenth, which is the intellect of the last sphere, manages the affairs of the world of elements according to the dispositions that accrue to elemental matters from the renewal of celestial configurations. By 'management of the intellects' is meant the effecting and bestowal of perfections, not the governance that belongs to souls with bodies.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage defines the number of the ten intellects and the roles of the first and tenth. It begins by stating the claim that the intellects are ten, in accordance with the number of spheres, but emphasizing that this is a lower bound (negating fewness) while not excluding abundance. The tenth intellect is specified as the manager of the sublunary world based on dispositions from celestial motions. It then notes a list of further attributes (eternal, species restricted to individuals, actual perfections, intellection of universals). The commentary explains that 'ten' means not less than ten, but more is not denied—the exact number is known only to God, because the number of spheres is not necessarily fixed at nine. It even allows for many spheres between the outer sphere and the sphere of fixed stars, and for each star to have its own sphere. The author then explains why the intellects become ten despite nine spheres: the First is a source for each sphere's intellect, soul, and sphere, so the emanated intellects are nine, making ten with the First. The tenth intellect manages the elemental world by bestowing perfections, not by bodily governance.

Key Terms
عقول
أفلاك
عقل العاشر
مدبر
العناصر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the intellects are exactly ten and no more.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that ten is a lower bound (negating fewness) and that more are possible, the true number being known only to Allah.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it stated that the intellects are ten despite the spheres being nine?
A) Because the first intellect is not counted among the nine emanating from it
B) Because the first sphere has no intellect
C) Because the tenth intellect manages the spheres
D) Because the spheres are actually ten in number

Key Takeaway
The intellects are at least ten, with the first as the source of emanation and the tenth governing the sublunary world by bestowing perfections from the celestial configurations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the tenth intellect manages the world by bestowing perfections according to celestial dispositions, then what do you truly rely on for your daily provisions? Are you aware of the chain of causes that Allah has put in place, or do you take them for granted?
?
The passage states that the intellects know only universals, not particulars. Yet Allah knows every detail of your life. How does that difference in knowledge affect your personal relationship with Him? Are you living as if He sees every particular, or as if He only knows generalities?
?
The philosophers said the intellects are immaterial and eternal. But you believe in a Creator who is eternal and immaterial. How does the difference between Creator and created change the way you direct your worship and reliance? Do you ever unintentionally attribute qualities of the Creator to His creation?

5 min
The Intellects Are Eternal
Proves the intellects are eternal because they lack material substratum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof for the eternality of the intellects based on their freedom from matter.

Core Idea
Freedom from matter proves the intellects have no beginning.

In this passage, the author presents a concise argument for the eternality of the intellects. The reasoning hinges on a general principle: everything that comes into existence is preceded by matter. Since the intellects are completely free from matter, they cannot be originated; hence they are eternal. Let's walk through the proof step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic sentence carefully. Notice its concise structure—it states the conclusion first, then the proof, then the exception.
The argument is compact; every word matters.
2
Identify the key principle
The proof relies on the principle that 'every originated thing is preceded by matter'. Understand what this means: to come into existence, something needs a material substratum.
3
Understand the two types of relation to matter
The passage mentions two ways an originated thing relates to matter: by indwelling (inherence) or by attachment. Identify examples: forms and accidents inhere; souls and intellects are attached.
4
Apply the principle to intellects
The intellects are described as 'free from that'—meaning they lack any relation to matter. Therefore, they cannot be originated and must be eternal.
Eternal here means without beginning, not just everlasting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها أنها أزلية لما سبق من أن كل حادث مسبوق بمادة، يحل فيها كالصور والأعراض، أو يتعلق بها كالنفوس والعقول مبرأة عن ذلك.
And among them [the attributes] is that they are eternal because of what has preceded—that every originated thing is preceded by matter, either indwelling in it like forms and accidents, or attached to it like souls and intellects—[while the intellects] are free from that.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage gives the proof for the eternality of the intellects. It states that the intellects are eternal because everything that comes into existence (hadith) is preceded by some matter that serves as its substratum—either the matter is a locus in which the thing inheres (like forms and accidents in physical substances) or to which it is attached (like souls and intellects to bodies). Since the intellects are free from both types of material relationship, they cannot be originated; therefore they are eternal. The argument relies on the principle that origination requires a prior material cause.

Each Intellect Is a Species with a Single Individual
Proves each intellect is a species with only one individual due to lack of matter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why each intellect is considered a unique species with only one individual, based on the principle that multiplicity of individuals requires matter.

Core Idea
Intellects are unique species because they lack matter to produce multiple individuals.

This lesson examines a key attribute of the intellects in Islamic cosmology: each intellect is a species that has only one individual. The reason lies in the nature of individuation, which depends on matter. By understanding this, we grasp the metaphysical distinction between material and immaterial beings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get the author's direct claim and proof.
Notice the concise style: a claim followed by an explanation.
2
Identify the key claim and its proof
The claim: 'each of the intellects is a species restricted to one individual'. The proof: 'multiplicity of individuals of a single species occurs only on account of matters and the dispositions that surround them.'
The proof is a general principle applied to intellects.
3
Understand the role of matter in multiplicity
Reflect on why matter is necessary for multiple individuals within a species. In material beings, different matter and dispositions produce different individuals. Intellects are immaterial, so no such differentiation occurs.
This connects to broader metaphysics: form and matter.
4
Reflect on the uniqueness of each intellect
Consider the implication: each intellect is a species unto itself, with no other individual sharing its essence. This sets intellects apart from material species like humans.
This also relates to the hierarchy of intellects in Neoplatonic cosmology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها أن كلا من العقول نوع ينحصر في شخص، لأن تكثر أشخاص النوع الواحد لا يكون إلا بحسب المواد، وما يكتنفها من الهيئات
And among them [the attributes] is that each of the intellects is a species restricted to one individual, because the multiplicity of individuals of a single species occurs only on account of matters and the dispositions that surround them.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage argues that each intellect constitutes a unique species that is fully realized in a single individual. The reason given is that the multiplication of individuals within a species (e.g., many human individuals within the human species) is caused by matter and the accompanying dispositions that differentiate individuals. Since the intellects are immaterial, there are no material factors that could produce multiple individuals under the same species; hence each species necessarily has only one member.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Correction: Each intellect is a species with a single individual because multiplicity requires matter, which intellects lack.

Checkpoint

A) Because there is no matter to produce multiple individuals
B) Because each intellect is a genus
C) Because they are all the same species
D) Because they are physical

Key Takeaway
Each intellect is a unique species with a single individual because the multiplication of individuals depends on matter and its dispositions, which are absent in the immaterial intellects.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are a soul united with a body. If your individuality is tied to matter and its dispositions, what does that say about the uniqueness of your soul? Are you living as a mere product of matter, or as a unique creation with a purpose that no one else can fulfill? What change must you make today to honor that uniqueness?
?
Each intellect is a species of one — utterly singular and irreplaceable. You are not an intellect, but your soul is also immaterial. Does your life reflect the gravity of being a one-of-a-kind creature of God? In what area of your life have you acted as if you are interchangeable or replaceable? Commit now to reject that lie and embrace your singular responsibility before your Creator.

The Perfections of the Intellects Are Actual
Sanusi proves the intellects' perfections are actual.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the perfections of the intellects are described as actual rather than potential, based on the impossibility of change in immaterial beings.

Core Idea
The intellects are perfect in actuality because they have no matter to enable change.

Sanusi argues that one attribute of the intellects is that their perfections are already actual. This may seem surprising, but he provides a concise proof based on the nature of potentiality and matter. Let's examine the argument carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once and then the English translation. Notice the concise structure: a claim followed by a proof.
2
Identify the logical components
Break down the sentence: the main claim is that the perfections are actual. The proof is given by the phrase after 'because'. Identify the key concepts: potentiality (قوة) and actuality (فعل), and the requirement of matter for transition.
The proof relies on the principle that change requires matter.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this matters for understanding the intellects. They are immaterial, so they cannot have unrealized potential. All their perfections are already present.
This reinforces the superiority and completeness of the celestial intellects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها أن كمالاتها حاصلة بالفعل، لأن خروج الشيء من القوة إلى الفعل، لا يكون إلا بما له مادة تندرج في الاستعدادات، بحسب تجدد المعدات من الأوضاع والحركات
And among them [the attributes] is that their perfections are actual, because the emergence of a thing from potentiality to actuality only occurs when it has matter that is subsumed under dispositions, according to the renewal of preparations from positions and motions.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage argues that the intellects possess their perfections (kamaalat) in actuality (bil-fi‘l), not potentially. The proof is that transition from potentiality (quwwa) to actuality (fi‘l) requires matter that receives successive dispositions through changes in positions and motions. Since the intellects are immaterial, they cannot undergo such a transition; therefore all their perfections are already fully realized.

Misconception & Correction

Correction: The passage argues that because the intellects have no matter, they cannot undergo change from potential to actual, so all their perfections are already actual and cannot increase.

Checkpoint

B) Because they are in constant motion
C) Because they are always potential
D) Because they are material

Key Takeaway
The intellects' perfections are fully realized because they lack matter, which is necessary for change from potential to actual.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have matter and can change, unlike the intellects. Are you actively moving from potential to actual in your faith and character, or are you stagnant? What specific step will you take today to actualize a good quality you know you have potential for?
?
The intellects are already perfect with no need for growth. Do you secretly wish you could be like that — free from struggle? Or do you embrace your state of potential, seeing it as a gift that allows you to earn reward? How does the reality of your own changeability affect your relationship with Allah today?

The Intellects Know Themselves and All Universals
Demonstrates the intellects know themselves and all universals without matter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the intellects, being immaterial, can know themselves through immediate presence and know all universals through the cooperative nature of intelligible forms.

Core Idea
The intellects know themselves by presence and all universals through immateriality.

This passage from Sharh al-Maqasid explains the remarkable cognitive capacity of the separate intellects. How can a non-physical entity know itself and everything universal? The author argues that because these intellects are pure immaterial forms, they are free from the limitations that prevent knowledge. You will see a careful argument about presence, cooperation of intelligible forms, and a rejection of circularity.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage carefully
First, read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the English translation. Notice how the argument moves from self-knowledge to knowledge of others.
The last line is incomplete; focus on the full argument before it.
2
Identify the two claims
The passage has two main theses: the intellects know themselves, and they know all universals. Notice the distinct proofs for each.
The proof for self-knowledge relies on immediate presence; the proof for universal knowledge relies on immateriality and non-opposition of forms.
3
Understand the argument about cooperation
The passage argues that intelligible forms are not mutually oppositional but cooperative. This allows multiple universals to be known together without conflict.
4
Grasp the anti-circularity reasoning
The passage rejects the idea that the validity of accompaniment depends on actual presence in the intellect, otherwise circularity. This establishes that the intellects can know universals even before those universals are actualized in the intellect.
This is a subtle logical point.
5
Reflect on the implication
Since the intellects exist actually, and whatever is possible for them is actual, they actually know themselves and all intelligibles. This is a key conclusion.
The passage ends with 'then you are aware of the foundation...' hinting at a continuation about particulars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها أنها عاقلة لذواتها، ولجميع الكليات. أما لذواتها، فلأنها حاضرة بماهياتها عند ذواتها المجردة، وهو معنى التعقل، إذ لا يتصور في تعقل الشيء لنفسه حصول المثال المطابق، وأما لغيرها، فلأنها مجردة، وكل مجرد يمكن أن يعقل لبراءته من الشوائب المادية، واللواحق الغريبة، المانعة عن التعقل، وكل ما يمكن أن يعقل، فإنه يمكن أن يعقل مع غيره من الكليات، لأن الصور العقلية ليست متعاندة، بل متعاونة، وكل ما يمكن أن يعقل مع غيره صح أن يقارنه من غير أن تتوقف صحة المقارنة على حصولهما في جوهر العاقل، لأن ذلك متأخر عن صحة المقارنة ضرورة تقدم إمكان الشيء على حصوله. فلو توقفت صحة المقارنة عليه لزم الدور. فإذن صحة مقارنة المجردات وسائر الكليات ثابتة عند حصول المجرد في الأعيان فيثبت صحة تعقله إياها، إذ لا معنى له سوى مقارنتها للمجرد وحضورها عنده وكل ما يصح للعقول المجردة، فهو حاصل بالفعل لما مر، فتكون عاقلة لذواتها، ولجميع المعقولات، ثم إنك خبير بابتناء
And among them [the attributes] is that they are intellective of themselves and of all universals. As for themselves, because they are present with their quiddities to their immaterial selves, and that is the meaning of intellection, for in the intellection of a thing by itself, the occurrence of a corresponding representation is inconceivable. As for others, because they are immaterial, and every immaterial entity can engage in intellection due to its being free from material impurities and extraneous attachments that prevent intellection; and everything that can engage in intellection can engage in intellection together with other universals because the intelligible forms are not mutually oppositional but rather cooperative. And everything that can be intellected together with another can be accompanied by it without the validity of the accompaniment depending on their occurrence in the substance of the intellect, because that [occurrence] is posterior to the validity of the accompaniment—since the possibility of a thing necessarily precedes its occurrence. If the validity of the accompaniment were dependent on it, there would be circularity. Therefore, the validity of the accompaniment of the immaterial [intellects] with the rest of the universals is established when the immaterial [intellect] occurs in re; thus the validity of its intellection of them is established, for there is no meaning to it other than their accompaniment of the immaterial and their presence with it. And everything that is valid for the immaterial intellects exists actually, as has passed, so they are intellective of themselves and of all intelligibles. Then you are aware of the foundation...
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage proves that the intellects are intellective of themselves and of all universals. It first explains self-intellection: the intellect's own essence is immediately present to itself without need for a mental representation. Then it addresses intellection of others: because the intellects are immaterial, they are free from material impurities that hinder intellection; thus they can engage in intellection. Furthermore, they can intellect universals together because intelligible forms are not mutually exclusive. The argument uses a principle that if something can be intellected, it can be intellected together with others, and the validity of such coexistence does not depend on actual presence in the intellect's substance—otherwise circularity arises. Since the intellects exist in actuality, their intellection of universals is actual. The passage concludes that they know themselves and all intelligibles. The final sentence 'Then you are aware of the foundation...' seems to introduce a new point, possibly about particulars, but the text cuts off.

Key Terms
عاقلة
ذوات
كليات
تعقل
صور عقلية
مقارنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Intellection always requires a mental representation that corresponds to the object.
Correction: For self-intellection, no representation is needed because the essence is immediately present. For intellection of universals, the forms are present in a cooperative manner without need for material images.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why can the intellects intellect all universals together?
A) Because intelligible forms are cooperative, not oppositional
B) Because they have material representations
C) Because each intellect is a separate species
D) Because they are physical entities

Key Takeaway
The intellects know themselves by immediate presence and all universals through their immateriality and the cooperative nature of intelligible forms.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You learn that the intellects know themselves by immediate presence, without any representation. In contrast, your own self-knowledge is often filtered through self-images and narratives. What false representations of yourself have you been carrying, and how can you begin to see your own quiddity directly?
?
The source states that immateriality frees intellect from material impurities that prevent true knowledge. What 'material impurities'—like desires, attachments, or biases—cloud your understanding of universal truths like justice, mercy, or God's attributes? Will you commit to purifying your heart to gain clearer intellection?
?
The argument shows that possibility must precede actuality; the validity of knowing universals is established before you actually know them. What good possibilities (e.g., virtues, knowledge) do you know are valid for you, yet you have not actualized? What is the one step you will take today to bring one such possibility into actuality?

The World of Similitudes and Its Rejection
The author discusses the world of similitudes and why verifiers ignore it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the concept of the world of similitudes in Islamic philosophy and why it was rejected by mainstream scholars.

Core Idea
The world of similitudes is a fanciful realm that fails rational and evidentiary scrutiny.

This passage introduces a controversial doctrine known as the world of similitudes (عالم المثل). The author presents its purported features and then explains why serious scholars dismissed it. You will see how weak arguments can lead to rejection even when backed by claimed miracles or dreams.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the vivid examples the author gives for the world of similitudes.
Pay special attention to the examples from dreams, illness, and saints.
2
Identify the arguments for this world
The passage mentions two types of evidence used by proponents: direct mystical experience (al-mukāshafa) and a rational syllogism about images in mirrors. Find these in the text.
3
Understand the author's verdict
Notice the conclusion: the claim is far-fetched and the evidence is weak, so the verifiers (al-muḥaqqiqūn) paid no attention. Reflect on why the arguments fail.
The author uses the phrase 'al-daʿwā ʿāliya wa al-shubha wāhiya'.
4
Evaluate the rejection
Consider whether the rejection is based on lack of evidence or on philosophical principles. Why would dreams and miracles not be sufficient proof?
This connects to broader principles in Islamic theology about verifying claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المعلقة نورانية فيها نعيم السعداء، وظلمانية فيها عذاب الأشقياء، وكذا أمر المنامات، وكثير من الإدراكات، فإن جميع ما يرى في المنام، أو يتخيل في اليقظة، بل يشاهد في الأمراض، وعند غلبة الخوف ونحو ذلك من الصور المقدارية، التي لا تحقق لها في عالم الحس كلها من عالم المثل، وكذا كثيراً من الغرائب وخوارق العادات، كما يحكى عن بعض الأولياء أنه مع إقامته ببلدته، كان من حاضري المسجد الحرام أيام الحج، وأنه ظهر من بعض جدران البيت، أو خرج من بيت مسدود الأبواب والكوات، وأنه أحضر بعض الأشخاص، أو الثمار، أو غير ذلك من مسافة بعيدة في زمان قريب إلى غير ذلك. والقائلون بهذا العالم منهم من يدعي نبوته بالمكاشفة والتجارب الصحيحة، ومنهم من يحتج بأن ما يشاهد من تلك الصور الجزئية في المرايا ونحوها، ليست عدماً صرفاً، ولا من عالم الماديات وهو ظاهر، ولا من عالم العقل لكونها ذوات مقدار ولا مرتسمة في الأجزاء الدماغية، لامتناع ارتسام الكبير في الصغير، ولما كانت الدعوى عالية والشبهة واهية. كما سبق لم يلتفت اليه المحققون من الحكماء والمتكلمين. والله أعلم.
The attached [world] is luminous, containing the bliss of the blessed, and dark, containing the torment of the wretched. Likewise is the matter of dreams and many perceptions, for everything seen in a dream, or imagined while awake, or even observed in illnesses and when fear dominates and similar [situations] – of those quantifiable images that have no realization in the sensory world – all are from the world of similitudes. Likewise many wonders and miraculous events, as is narrated about some saints that while residing in their town, they were among those present in the Sacred Mosque during the days of Hajj, and that he appeared from some walls of the house, or came out of a house with sealed doors and windows, and that he brought some persons, or fruits, or other things from a distant place in a short time, and so forth. Those who affirm this world: some claim knowledge of it through unveiling and sound experiments; others argue that what is observed of those particular images in mirrors and the like are neither sheer nothingness, nor from the material world – which is obvious – nor from the world of intellect, because they have magnitude and are not imprinted in the brain's parts, due to the impossibility of imprinting the large in the small. But since the claim is far-fetched and the doubt is feeble, as before, the verifiers among the philosophers and theologians did not pay attention to it. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage presents the concept of the 'world of similitudes' (عالم المثل) and evaluates it. The author first describes this world as having a luminous aspect for the blessed and a dark aspect for the wretched. He then provides examples: everything seen in dreams, waking imaginations, and even some perceptions during illness or fear are said to belong to this world. Further, wonders and miracles, such as a saint being present in Mecca while staying in his hometown, or objects appearing from sealed places, are attributed to it. Next, the author reports two arguments of those who affirm this world: some claim direct knowledge through unveiling and experience; others offer a syllogism: the images seen in mirrors are not nothing, not material (obviously), and not intellectual (because they have magnitude and are not imprinted in the brain due to size impossibility). However, the author concludes that since the claim is far-fetched and the doubt is feeble, the verifiers (المحققون) among philosophers and theologians dismissed it. The passage thus rejects the world of similitudes as an unsupported doctrine.

Key Terms
عالم المثل
الصور المقدارية
المحققون
المكاشفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The world of similitudes is a proven realm based on dreams and miracles.
Correction: The author shows that the examples are not reliable evidence and the arguments are weak, so verifiers reject it.

Checkpoint
Why did the verifiers (المحققون) not pay attention to the world of similitudes?
A) Because the examples are not miraculous.
B) Because the claim is far-fetched and the evidence is weak.
C) Because they did not believe in dreams.
D) Because the images in mirrors are material.

Key Takeaway
The world of similitudes is rejected by verifiers because its claims are far-fetched and its evidence weak.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever been captivated by a dream or a seemingly miraculous story to the point that you built a belief upon it? How does this lesson's dismissal of such evidence as 'far-fetched' challenge you to re-evaluate what you consider reliable knowledge?
?
The verifiers (المحققون) are described as those who did not pay attention to weak proofs. In your own search for truth, are there claims you hold onto that are based on feeling or tradition rather than solid evidence? Will you be willing to let them go as the verifiers did?
?
This passage says that many perceptions (dreams, imaginations, fears) are from the world of similitudes but have no realization in the sensory world. When you experience vivid dreams or strong imaginations, do you tend to ascribe real significance to them? How can you distinguish between what is true and what is merely a similitude?
